The Necessity of Qiyas in Knowing the Maker
Maturidi argues for the necessity of qiyas in knowing the Maker.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi argues that qiyas (analogical reasoning) is indispensable for theological knowledge of Allah.

Core Idea
Without qiyas, knowledge of the unseen Maker is impossible.

Maturidi begins by addressing the role of qiyas in theology. He argues that if qiyas is not used, then the Mu'tazilite method of knowing the Maker through reason alone collapses, because the senses cannot reach Allah. This sets the stage for his proof that all actions are created by Allah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disjunction
Read the first sentence: Maturidi presents two possibilities: either qiyas is used or it is not. Notice how he frames this as a logical necessity.
This is a common kalam technique to narrow down options.
2
Trace the consequence of not using qiyas
If qiyas is not used, the opponents' method of knowing the Maker fails because Allah is beyond sensory perception. Therefore, qiyas must be used.
Maturidi is countering those who rely solely on empirical evidence.
3
Understand the inference from the witnessed
Maturidi states that qiyas is based on inference from the witnessed (shahid) to the unseen. He observes that all meanings found in the world are also present in human actions.
This establishes a common ground between observable actions and divine creation.
4
Consider the alternative via revelation
If actions are not created by Allah, then only revelation (sam') can tell us about creation, leading to the necessity of the general verse 'Creator of everything' (Quran 6:102).
This shows that either qiyas or the general scriptural statement forces the conclusion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأيضاً إن القياس مما لا يخلو من أن يكون مستعملاً فيما نحن فيه أو لا؛ فإن كان لا يستعمل بطل مذهب الخصوم في معرفة الصانع، لارتفاع الحواس عنه، فيجب معرفته بذلك، وهو على الاستدلال بالشاهد ثم نجد جميع المعاني التي هي للعالم بأعراضه موجودة في أفعال الخلق . فلئن لم يجب القول بخلقها لم يجز معرفة خلق ألبتة إلا بالسمع، فيجب به استعمال العموم بقوله : خالق كل شيء ﴾ [الأنعام، ١٠٢/٦]، إذ لا سبيل إلى وجود خلق كل شيء باسم الخاصية له، أو يلزم القول بالقياس من الوجه الذي ذكر . ثم لم يصر العبد بفعله خالقاً ، ثبت أنه بغيره . مع ما إذ كان سبيل معرفة الفاعل إنما هو بآثار الفعل . ثم كان الإيمان من أحسن الأفعال في العقول وأنور الأشياء وأتمها وأجلّها قدرًا وأثبتها لمرضاته. فلو قلنا: إن الله غير خالق له دخل علينا أمران في ذلك أحدهما تفضيل من يطيع الله بالإيمان وغيره على الله بما خلق من الأقذار والأنتان والخبائث والقبائح من الجواهر؛ مع ما كان ما حَسُن من الجواهر لا يبلغ قدر الذي ذكر من [الإيمان و] العبادات في الحسن والخير. وإذا كان كذلك - ومعلوم تفاضل الفاضلين بتفاضل أفعالهم - أوجب ذلك فضل العبد على الله في الفعل والخلق. وهذا بالمعتزلة أولى، لأنهم زعموا أن فعل الكفر قبيح شر من جميع الوجوه، وليس كذلك أمر القردة [۱۲۲] والخنازير، فمثله فعل الإيمان [خير] من جميع جواهر الحسان ولا قوة إلا بالله . / والثاني أن ثوابه إذ حُسنه حستى وحسن الايمان عقلي، وما حسن في الحس دون الذي يحسن في العقل، إذ قد يجوز انقلاب مثله على ما مربيانه، ولا يجوز انقلاب الآخر. وإذا كان كذلك فيقتصر الجزاء على قدر المجزي [به]، والله وعد جزاء الحسنة بعشر أمثالها ، ثبت أن خلق فعل الإيمان حسنا الله ولا قوة إلا بالله . وبعد، فإن الله تعالى ذم الذين يحبون أن يُحمدوا بما لم يفعلوا ، ثم ألزم عباده الشكر له على الإيمان، والحمد لله على الإنعام؛ لم يجز أن يكون غير خالق لذلك فيَستَأدى الحمد له على الإيمان، والحمد لله على الإنعام؛ لم يجز أن يكون غير خالق لذلك فيَستَأدى الحمد له على الإيمان، والحمد لله على الإنعام؛
And also, qiyas (analogical reasoning) is not free from being used in what we are discussing or not. If it is not used, then the doctrine of the opponents concerning knowledge of the Maker becomes invalid, because the senses are removed from Him; so knowledge of Him must be by that (i.e., qiyas). And it is based on inference from the witnessed (shahid). Then we find all the meanings which belong to the world with its accidents existing in the actions of creatures. So if it is not necessary to say that they are created, then knowledge of creation (khilq) would not be possible at all except through revelation (sam'), and therefore it is necessary to use the general statement (al-umum) by His saying: "Creator of everything" [Quran 6:102], since there is no way for the existence of creation of everything by the name of particularity for Him, or it necessitates the use of qiyas from the mentioned aspect. Then, since the servant does not become a creator by his act, it is established that it is by another. Moreover, since the way to know the agent is only through the traces of the act, and then faith (iman) is among the best of actions in the intellects, the most luminous of things, the most perfect, the greatest in worth, and the most confirming for His pleasure—so if we say that Allah is not its creator, two matters enter upon us in that. One of them: preferring the one who obeys Allah by faith and others over Allah, by what is created of filth, stench, evil and ugly things from substances (jawahir); whereas what is good from the substances does not reach the level of what was mentioned of [faith and] acts of worship in goodness and virtue. And if that is so—and it is known that the superiority of two excellent ones is by the superiority of their actions—that necessitates the servant's virtue over Allah in action and creation. And this applies more to the Mu'tazilites, because they claimed that the act of disbelief is ugly and evil in every respect, and not so is the case of apes and pigs; similarly, the act of faith is [better] than all beautiful substances. And there is no power except with Allah. / And the second: that its reward, since its goodness is good and the goodness of faith is rational (aqli), and what is good in sense (hiss) is not like what is good in the intellect, for it is possible that the like of it changes as we have seen, but the other does not change. And if that is so, then the recompense is limited to the measure of the requited [by it], and Allah promised the reward of a good deed ten times its like. So it is established that the creation of the act of faith is good by Allah. And there is no power except with Allah. Thereafter, Allah the Exalted has condemned those who love to be praised for what they have not done, and then He obligated His servants to thank Him for faith, and praise be to Allah for blessings; it is not possible that He is not the creator of that, for then He would be soliciting praise for faith, and praise be to Allah for blessings; it is not possible that He is not the creator of that, for then He would be soliciting praise for faith, and praise be to Allah for blessings.
Source pages p. 313

Commentary
This passage is a complex proof (using qiyas, empirical observation, and scriptural appeal) that Allah creates all actions, with a special focus on the act of faith (iman). Maturidi begins by discussing the role of qiyas (analogical reasoning): either it is used in this matter or not. If it is not used, then the opponents' (Mu'tazilites) method of knowing the Maker fails, because sensory knowledge is impossible; thus qiyas must be used. The method is inference from the witnessed (shahid) to the unseen. We observe that all meanings (properties) found in the world and its accidents are also present in the actions of creatures. Therefore, if these actions are not created by Allah, then knowledge of creation would be limited to revelation alone, which then necessitates using the general statement "Creator of everything" (Quran 6:102) literally, since there is no other way to attribute creation to Him. Alternatively, if qiyas is used, it leads to the same conclusion: the servant does not become a creator by his act, so the act is created by another (Allah). Maturidi then focuses on iman, the best action. If Allah were not its creator, two absurdities follow. First, it would imply preferring the obedient servant over Allah, because the servant would create an excellent action (iman) while Allah creates only vile things like filth and ugly substances. Since excellence is in actions, the servant would surpass Allah in virtue—an impossibility. He notes this is especially true for the Mu'tazilites, who deem disbelief supremely evil; similarly, iman surpasses all good substances. Second, the reward for iman is based on its rational goodness; but if its goodness were merely sensory, it could change, but rational goodness does not. Since reward is proportional to the act, and Allah promises tenfold reward, this shows that the act of iman is created good by Allah. Finally, Maturidi adds an argument from the Quran: Allah condemns those who love praise for what they have not done, and He requires thankfulness to Him for faith. If Allah did not create faith, He would be praising Himself for something He did not create, which is impossible. Thus, Allah must be the creator of iman.

Key Terms
قياس
شاهد
خالق كل شيء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think qiyas is unnecessary in theology because Allah can be known through pure reason or scripture alone.
Correction: Maturidi shows that without qiyas, knowledge of the Maker is impossible because He is beyond sensory experience; even scripture presupposes qiyas for inference to the unseen.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the consequence if qiyas is not used in theology?
A) The opponents' method of knowing the Maker becomes invalid.
B) Knowledge of the Maker becomes easier through senses.
C) The general verse 'Creator of everything' cannot be used.
D) Nothing changes.

Key Takeaway
Qiyas is necessary for knowing the unseen Maker because sensory knowledge is impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever felt that your faith relies too much on what you can see and touch? How does Maturidi’s argument that sensory knowledge cannot reach the Maker challenge you to use your intellect in a way you haven't before? What will you do this week to strengthen your reliance on rational inference in your belief in Allah?
?
When you observe the world around you, do you consciously connect the accidents (like color, motion, sound) to the Creator, or do you take them for granted? This passage says that these are signs pointing to Allah. Where in your daily life do you overlook these signs, and how can you train yourself to see them as arguments for His existence?
?
The passage presents qiyas as unavoidable for knowing the unseen. If you were to explain to a skeptic why reason must be used to know God, would you use this argument? What makes it compelling, and what would you say if they reject the need for inference? Commit to sharing this reasoning with someone who doubts.

The Creation of Actions and the Excellence of Iman
Maturidi proves actions are created by Allah and extols iman.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses the observed fact that actions contain meanings similar to the world to prove they are created by Allah, and why iman is the most excellent action.

Core Idea
Since the servant does not become a creator, his actions must be created by Allah.

Maturidi continues the qiyas argument by focusing on the traces of actions. He argues that the way to know the agent is through the effects. Actions have observable meanings, so they must have a creator. Since humans do not create their own actions, Allah must be the creator. He then highlights that iman, the act of faith, is the best and most luminous action.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the two logical steps: servant not becoming creator, and the excellence of iman.
The passage is concise but packed with meaning.
2
Understand the inference from traces
Maturidi says the way to know the agent is through the traces of the act. Since we see actions, they must have an agent. The servant does not create his own act, so the agent is Allah.
This is an application of the qiyas from the previous lesson.
3
Reflect on the nature of iman
Iman is described as the best, most luminous, most perfect action. Why does Maturidi emphasize this? Because if such an excellent act is not created by Allah, it would lead to absurdities (next lesson).
This sets up the argument for the necessity of Allah creating iman.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And also, qiyas (analogical reasoning) is not free from being used in what we are discussing or not. If it is not used, then the doctrine of the opponents concerning knowledge of the Maker becomes invalid, because the senses are removed from Him; so knowledge of Him must be by that (i.e., qiyas). And it is based on inference from the witnessed (shahid). Then we find all the meanings which belong to the world with its accidents existing in the actions of creatures. So if it is not necessary to say that they are created, then knowledge of creation (khilq) would not be possible at all except through revelation (sam'), and therefore it is necessary to use the general statement (al-umum) by His saying: "Creator of everything" [Quran 6:102], since there is no way for the existence of creation of everything by the name of particularity for Him, or it necessitates the use of qiyas from the mentioned aspect. And if that is so—and it is known that the superiority of two excellent ones is by the superiority of their actions—that necessitates the servant's virtue over Allah in action and creation. Commentary
This passage is a complex proof (using qiyas, empirical observation, and scriptural appeal) that Allah creates all actions, with a special focus on the act of faith (iman). Maturidi begins by discussing the role of qiyas (analogical reasoning): either it is used in this matter or not. If it is not used, then the opponents' (Mu'tazilites) method of knowing the Maker fails, because sensory knowledge is impossible; thus qiyas must be used. The method is inference from the witnessed (shahid) to the unseen. We observe that all meanings (properties) found in the world and its accidents are also present in the actions of creatures. Therefore, if these actions are not created by Allah, then knowledge of creation would be limited to revelation alone, which then necessitates using the general statement "Creator of everything" (Quran 6:102) literally, since there is no other way to attribute creation to Him. Alternatively, if qiyas is used, it leads to the same conclusion: the servant does not become a creator by his act, so the act is created by another (Allah). Maturidi then focuses on iman, the best action. If Allah were not its creator, two absurdities follow. First, it would imply preferring the obedient servant over Allah, because the servant would create an excellent action (iman) while Allah creates only vile things like filth and ugly substances. Since excellence is in actions, the servant would surpass Allah in virtue—an impossibility. He notes this is especially true for the Mu'tazilites, who deem disbelief supremely evil; similarly, iman surpasses all good substances. Second, the reward for iman is based on its rational goodness; but if its goodness were merely sensory, it could change, but rational goodness does not. Since reward is proportional to the act, and Allah promises tenfold reward, this shows that the act of iman is created good by Allah. Finally, Maturidi adds an argument from the Quran: Allah condemns those who love praise for what they have not done, and He requires thankfulness to Him for faith. If Allah did not create faith, He would be praising Himself for something He did not create, which is impossible. Thus, Allah must be the creator of iman.

Key Terms
إيمان
فعل
خالق

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why must actions be created by Allah?
A) Because the servant does not become a creator by his act.
B) Because actions have no traces.
C) Because iman is the worst action.
D) Because the senses directly perceive Allah.

Key Takeaway
Because the servant does not create his own act, it must be created by Allah, especially the excellent act of faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your faith is not your own creation but a gift from Allah, how does that change the way you view your spiritual achievements? Will you take credit for your iman or thank Allah more deeply?
?
The passage says iman is 'the most luminous of things'. What darkness in your life are you still clinging to despite the light of faith? What step will you take today to let that light expose and heal one hidden sin?
?
Since actions reveal the agent, what does the state of your iman reveal about your relationship with Allah right now? If it is weak, are you content to leave it that way, or will you beg the Creator to renew it in your heart this moment?

The Two Absurdities and the Quranic Argument
Maturidi presents two absurdities and a Quranic argument for Allah creating iman.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two absurdities that follow if Allah were not the creator of iman, and the Quranic argument that Allah obligates thankfulness for faith.

Core Idea
If Allah did not create iman, the servant would be superior to Allah and reward would be unjust.

Maturidi now presents two devastating consequences if one denies that Allah creates the act of faith. First, it would imply the servant creates something better than any good creature, making the servant superior to Allah. Second, the rational goodness of iman would not change, proving its divine origin. He then adds a Quranic argument: Allah requires gratitude for faith, impossible if He did not create it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two 'amran' (matters)
Maturidi says 'two matters enter upon us'. Read carefully to find both absurdities. The first is about superiority, the second about reward.
The Arabic uses 'ahaduhuma' and 'al-thani'.
2
Analyze the first absurdity
If the servant creates iman, which is better than any good substance created by Allah, then the servant would be superior in virtue. Maturidi notes this especially applies to the Mu'tazilites.
This is a reductio ad absurdum.
3
Analyze the second absurdity
The goodness of iman is rational and immutable, unlike sensory goodness. Reward is proportional, and Allah promises tenfold reward, showing iman's goodness is created by Allah.
This argument links the nature of goodness to divine recompense.
4
Understand the Quranic argument
Allah condemns being praised for what one didn't do and requires thankfulness for iman. If Allah did not create iman, He would be soliciting praise for something He didn't create, which is impossible.
This is a direct scriptural proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأيضاً إن القياس مما لا يخلو من أن يكون مستعملاً فيما نحن فيه أو لا؛ فإن كان لا يستعمل بطل مذهب الخصوم في معرفة الصانع، لارتفاع الحواس عنه، فيجب معرفته بذلك، وهو على الاستدلال بالشاهد ثم نجد جميع المعاني التي هي للعالم بأعراضه موجودة في أفعال الخلق . فلئن لم يجب القول بخلقها لم يجز معرفة خلق ألبتة إلا بالسمع، فيجب به استعمال العموم بقوله : خالق كل شيء ﴾ [الأنعام، ١٠٢/٦]، إذ لا سبيل إلى وجود خلق كل شيء باسم الخاصية له، أو يلزم القول بالقياس من الوجه الذي ذكر . ثم لم يصر العبد بفعله خالقاً ، ثبت أنه بغيره . مع ما إذ كان سبيل معرفة الفاعل إنما هو بآثار الفعل . ثم كان الإيمان من أحسن الأفعال في العقول وأنور الأشياء وأتمها وأجلّها قدرًا وأثبتها لمرضاته. فلو قلنا: إن الله غير خالق له دخل علينا أمران في ذلك أحدهما تفضيل من يطيع الله بالإيمان وغيره على الله بما خلق من الأقذار والأنتان والخبائث والقبائح من الجواهر؛ مع ما كان ما حَسُن من الجواهر لا يبلغ قدر الذي ذكر من [الإيمان و] العبادات في الحسن والخير. وإذا كان كذلك - ومعلوم تفاضل الفاضلين بتفاضل أفعالهم - أوجب ذلك فضل العبد على الله في الفعل والخلق. وهذا بالمعتزلة أولى، لأنهم زعموا أن فعل الكفر قبيح شر من جميع الوجوه، وليس كذلك أمر القردة [۱۲۲] والخنازير، فمثله فعل الإيمان [خير] من جميع جواهر الحسان ولا قوة إلا بالله . / والثاني أن ثوابه إذ حُسنه حستى وحسن الايمان عقلي، وما حسن في الحس دون الذي يحسن في العقل، إذ قد يجوز انقلاب مثله على ما مربيانه، ولا يجوز انقلاب الآخر. وإذا كان كذلك فيقتصر الجزاء على قدر المجزي [به]، والله وعد جزاء الحسنة بعشر أمثالها ، ثبت أن خلق فعل الإيمان حسنا الله ولا قوة إلا بالله . وبعد، فإن الله تعالى ذم الذين يحبون أن يُحمدوا بما لم يفعلوا ، ثم ألزم عباده الشكر له على الإيمان، والحمد لله على الإنعام؛ لم يجز أن يكون غير خالق لذلك فيَستَأدى الحمد له على الإيمان، والحمد لله على الإنعام؛ لم يجز أن يكون غير خالق لذلك فيَستَأدى الحمد له على الإيمان، والحمد لله على الإنعام؛
And also, qiyas (analogical reasoning) is not free from being used in what we are discussing or not. If it is not used, then the doctrine of the opponents concerning knowledge of the Maker becomes invalid, because the senses are removed from Him; so knowledge of Him must be by that (i.e., qiyas). And it is based on inference from the witnessed (shahid). Then we find all the meanings which belong to the world with its accidents existing in the actions of creatures. So if it is not necessary to say that they are created, then knowledge of creation (khilq) would not be possible at all except through revelation (sam'), and therefore it is necessary to use the general statement (al-umum) by His saying: "Creator of everything" [Quran 6:102], since there is no way for the existence of creation of everything by the name of particularity for Him, or it necessitates the use of qiyas from the mentioned aspect. Then, since the servant does not become a creator by his act, it is established that it is by another. Moreover, since the way to know the agent is only through the traces of the act, and then faith (iman) is among the best of actions in the intellects, the most luminous of things, the most perfect, the greatest in worth, and the most confirming for His pleasure—so if we say that Allah is not its creator, two matters enter upon us in that. One of them: preferring the one who obeys Allah by faith and others over Allah, by what is created of filth, stench, evil and ugly things from substances (jawahir); whereas what is good from the substances does not reach the level of what was mentioned of [faith and] acts of worship in goodness and virtue. And if that is so—and it is known that the superiority of two excellent ones is by the superiority of their actions—that necessitates the servant's virtue over Allah in action and creation. And this applies more to the Mu'tazilites, because they claimed that the act of disbelief is ugly and evil in every respect, and not so is the case of apes and pigs; similarly, the act of faith is [better] than all beautiful substances. And there is no power except with Allah. / And the second: that its reward, since its goodness is good and the goodness of faith is rational (aqli), and what is good in sense (hiss) is not like what is good in the intellect, for it is possible that the like of it changes as we have seen, but the other does not change. And if that is so, then the recompense is limited to the measure of the requited [by it], and Allah promised the reward of a good deed ten times its like. So it is established that the creation of the act of faith is good by Allah. And there is no power except with Allah. Thereafter, Allah the Exalted has condemned those who love to be praised for what they have not done, and then He obligated His servants to thank Him for faith, and praise be to Allah for blessings; it is not possible that He is not the creator of that, for then He would be soliciting praise for faith, and praise be to Allah for blessings; it is not possible that He is not the creator of that, for then He would be soliciting praise for faith, and praise be to Allah for blessings.
Source pages p. 313

Commentary
This passage is a complex proof (using qiyas, empirical observation, and scriptural appeal) that Allah creates all actions, with a special focus on the act of faith (iman). Maturidi begins by discussing the role of qiyas (analogical reasoning): either it is used in this matter or not. If it is not used, then the opponents' (Mu'tazilites) method of knowing the Maker fails, because sensory knowledge is impossible; thus qiyas must be used. The method is inference from the witnessed (shahid) to the unseen. We observe that all meanings (properties) found in the world and its accidents are also present in the actions of creatures. Therefore, if these actions are not created by Allah, then knowledge of creation would be limited to revelation alone, which then necessitates using the general statement "Creator of everything" (Quran 6:102) literally, since there is no other way to attribute creation to Him. Alternatively, if qiyas is used, it leads to the same conclusion: the servant does not become a creator by his act, so the act is created by another (Allah). Maturidi then focuses on iman, the best action. If Allah were not its creator, two absurdities follow. First, it would imply preferring the obedient servant over Allah, because the servant would create an excellent action (iman) while Allah creates only vile things like filth and ugly substances. Since excellence is in actions, the servant would surpass Allah in virtue—an impossibility. He notes this is especially true for the Mu'tazilites, who deem disbelief supremely evil; similarly, iman surpasses all good substances. Second, the reward for iman is based on its rational goodness; but if its goodness were merely sensory, it could change, but rational goodness does not. Since reward is proportional to the act, and Allah promises tenfold reward, this shows that the act of iman is created good by Allah. Finally, Maturidi adds an argument from the Quran: Allah condemns those who love praise for what they have not done, and He requires thankfulness to Him for faith. If Allah did not create faith, He would be praising Himself for something He did not create, which is impossible. Thus, Allah must be the creator of iman.

Correction: Maturidi shows this leads to absurdities: the servant would be superior to Allah in creating virtuous acts, and the reward would not be proportional to a divinely created goodness.

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

The Self-Evident Nature of Human Freedom
Maturidi rejects jabr by appealing to self-evident human freedom.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi argues that the claim of necessity (jabr) is invalid because it contradicts self-evident knowledge that humans are free.

Core Idea
Everyone knows they are free; claiming necessity denies self-evident truth.

Maturidi begins his refutation of the doctrine of compulsion (jabr) by appealing to what every person knows intuitively: that they have choice. He argues that the claim of necessity is not only false but absurd, because it goes against the most basic self-awareness. In this lesson, we examine his opening argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the forceful opening: 'invalid and corrupt'.
2
Identify the key claim
Maturidi says everyone knows they are free (mukhtar). This is the core of his argument.
3
Understand the reductio ad absurdum
He argues that if one could claim the opposite based on inner feeling, then any such claim would be permissible, leading to absurdity.
4
Reflect on self-evident knowledge
Ask yourself: why is self-evident knowledge considered a reliable foundation in theological argumentation?
This connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ج وأما القول بإيجاب الضرورة فإنه محال فاسد، لأنه حتى أن يعلم كل أنه مختار، ولو جاز القول مما يعلمه كل على جهة قلبه الجاز ذلك في جميع العالم. ولا قوة إلا بالله . فإن قلت: إذ لم يوجب الضرورة دلّ أنه لا تدبير فيه لغيرك. قيل : قد فرغنا عن دلالة ذلك؛ مع ما يجوز أن يقال : هو من طريق الخلق اضطرار، ولا ذلك الوجه إذ لا يسمى به ، ومن طريق الكسب اختيار، فعلى ذلك تقسيم للعبد من صنع للعبد الأمرين، وقد بيّنا . ألا ترى أن قول الكفر كذب، وهو من حيث الدلالة على سفه القائل صدق. فمثله يكون اختيارا من حيث الكسب، ومن حيث الخلق لا؛ وجهة الخلق لا تدفع عنه الاختيار بما ثبت فسواء لو كان خلق ذلك الفعل أو خلق السماء والأرض، إذ ليس في واحد صرف فعل الخلق عن الخلق، ولا إزالة الاختيار عنهم؛ فمثله خلق الأفعال. ولا قوة إلا بالله على أن تسمية الخلق لا يوجب وصف الاضطرار، إذ القدرة للفعل مخلوقة، وهي سبب جعله مختارا لا مضطرا ولا قوة إلا بالله .
And as for the statement of necessitating necessity, it is invalid and corrupt, because everyone knows that he is free (mukhtar), and if it were permissible to say what everyone knows by way of his heart, then that would be permissible in the entire world. And there is no power except with Allah. If you say: 'Since it does not necessitate necessity, it indicates that there is no governance (tadbir) in it for other than you.' It is said: We have already finished with the proof of that; along with what may be said: It is from the perspective of creation (khalq) necessity (idtirar), and that aspect is not called by that name, and from the perspective of acquisition (kasb) it is choice (ikhtiyar). So on that basis there is a division for the servant from the making of the two matters, and we have explained. Do you not see that the statement of disbelief (kufr) is false, but from the perspective of indicating the foolishness of the speaker it is true. Similarly, it is choice from the perspective of acquisition, and from the perspective of creation it is not; the aspect of creation does not remove choice from it according to what has been established. So it is the same whether He created that action or created the heavens and the earth, since there is not in one of them the turning away of the creation of action from the created, nor the removal of choice from them; similarly is the creation of actions. And there is no power except with Allah. Moreover, calling it 'creation' does not necessitate the description of compulsion, since the power (qudra) for the action is created, and it is the cause of making him free (mukhtar) not compelled (mudtar). And there is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the claim that human actions are necessitated (jabr). Maturidi begins by stating that the claim of necessity is invalid because every person knows intuitively that they are free and make choices. If one were to claim that everyone knows something by heart that contradicts this, it would lead to absurdity. Then he addresses an objection: if actions are not necessitated, then there is no governance in them. He responds by distinguishing between two aspects: from the perspective of creation (khalq) the action is according to God's will and creation, which is a kind of necessity, but from the perspective of acquisition (kasb) the action is the servant's choice. These two aspects do not contradict each other. He gives an example: the statement of disbelief is itself false, but as an indicator of the speaker's foolishness it is true. Similarly, an action is chosen from the aspect of acquisition, but not from the aspect of creation. The aspect of creation does not negate choice. He clarifies that whether God creates the action or creates the heavens and earth, it does not negate the servant's choice. Finally, he emphasizes that calling God's creation of actions 'creation' does not imply compulsion for the servant, because the power (qudra) for the action is also created by God, and that power is what makes the servant free, not compelled.

الضرورة
الاضطرار
المختار
قول الكفر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If God controls everything, humans have no choice.
Correction: Maturidi argues that self-awareness of choice is undeniable, so even if God is the ultimate creator, humans still experience freedom.

Checkpoint
Why does Maturidi say the claim of necessity is 'invalid and corrupt'?
A) Because it contradicts revelation
B) Because everyone knows they are free
C) Because it denies God's power
D) Because the Quran explicitly denies it

Key Takeaway
Maturidi refutes jabr by grounding his argument in the universal self-knowledge of human freedom.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You claim to have free will, but have you ever made an excuse for your sin by blaming your circumstances or even God's decree? Read Maturidi's words: 'everyone knows that he is free.' Is that knowledge alive in your heart when you sin, or do you suppress it to avoid accountability? This week, catch yourself every time you shift blame and instead own your free choice.
?
If you truly believe that Allah has given you free will, then why do you sometimes feel powerless to obey? Is it because you have convinced yourself that your desires are stronger than your resolve? Reflect on a specific command of Allah that you have been neglecting, and write down one step you can take tomorrow to exercise your free will in obedience.

Reconciling Divine Creation with Human Choice
Maturidi explains the compatibility of divine creation and human acquisition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses the distinction between khalq (creation) and kasb (acquisition) to reconcile God's creation of actions with human responsibility.

Core Idea
Actions are both created by God and acquired by humans – two aspects, no contradiction.

After the initial refutation, Maturidi anticipates an objection: if actions are not necessitated, does that mean God has no governance? He responds by distinguishing two perspectives: from God’s perspective, actions are created (khalq); from the human perspective, they are acquired (kasb). This lesson unpacks that distinction and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
The questioner argues: if actions are not necessary, then there is no tadbir (governance) for anyone but you. This challenges divine sovereignty.
2
See Maturidi's response
He dismisses the objection briefly, then introduces the two aspects: creation (khalq) and acquisition (kasb).
The phrase 'قد فرغنا عن دلالة ذلك' indicates he already proved the point.
3
Grasp the khalq/kasb distinction
From the perspective of creation, it is necessity; from acquisition, it is choice. These are not contradictory but complementary.
4
Analyze the example
The statement of kufr is false in itself but true as an indicator of foolishness – illustrating dual aspects without contradiction.
5
Conclude: created power enables choice
Maturidi ends by noting that calling something creation does not imply compulsion; the created power (qudra) makes the human free.
Reflect on how this resolves the theological tension.

Source Text

So on that basis there is a division for the servant from the making of the two matters, and we have explained. Do you not see that the statement of disbelief (kufr) is false, but from the perspective of indicating the foolishness of the speaker it is true. Similarly, it is choice from the perspective of acquisition, and from the perspective of creation it is not; the aspect of creation does not remove choice from it according to what has been established. So it is the same whether He created that action or created the heavens and the earth, since there is not in one of them the turning away of the creation of action from the created, nor the removal of choice from them; similarly is the creation of actions. And there is no power except with Allah. Moreover, calling it 'creation' does not necessitate the description of compulsion, since the power (qudra) for the action is created, and it is the cause of making him free (mukhtar) not compelled (mudtar). Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the claim that human actions are necessitated (jabr). Maturidi begins by stating that the claim of necessity is invalid because every person knows intuitively that they are free and make choices. If one were to claim that everyone knows something by heart that contradicts this, it would lead to absurdity. Then he addresses an objection: if actions are not necessitated, then there is no governance in them. Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If God creates an action, then the human is compelled.
Correction: Maturidi shows that creation (khalq) is one aspect, acquisition (kasb) another; the creation aspect does not remove choice.

Checkpoint
What does Maturidi mean by 'from the perspective of creation (khalq) it is necessity, and from the perspective of acquisition (kasb) it is choice'?
A) That some actions are created by God and some by humans
B) That actions have two aspects without contradiction
C) That necessity overrides choice
D) That acquisition is an illusion

Key Takeaway
Maturidi reconciles divine predestination and human free will by distinguishing the perspective of creation from that of acquisition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you commit a sin, do you truly believe that Allah created that action, yet you are fully responsible? Examine your heart: is there a part of you that uses divine creation as an excuse to avoid accountability? What would change if you genuinely accepted both aspects without shifting blame?
?
Think of a moment when you felt completely out of control, as if you were compelled by circumstances. How does Maturidi's teaching that the power for action is itself created and is the cause of your choice challenge that feeling? Will you now see that moment differently and own your role in it?
?
If every action, including your worship and your sins, is created by Allah, do you still feel genuine freedom? Search yourself: do you resent that thought, or does it humble you? What does this passage demand of you in your next moment of decision?

The Act of Insult: Blame Attaches to the Doer, Not the Creator
Maturidi refutes the idea that creating an insult makes God blameworthy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why God is not blameworthy for creating an evil act; rather, blame attaches to the one who performs the act.

Core Idea
God's creation of an act does not transfer its blame to Him.

In this passage, Imam Maturidi counters a Mu'tazili argument that if God creates an insult, He becomes insulted. He shows that the act itself, being an accident, is not inherently insulting, and blame belongs to the doer. This lesson unpacks that key distinction.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation to grasp the overall argument.
The Arabic may be challenging due to OCR issues.
2
Identify the Mu'tazili claim
Find where Maturidi states the opponent's argument that God's creation of an insult makes Him blameworthy.
3
Analyse the analogy
Notice the comparison between knowing the act correctly (wise) vs. as the disbeliever sees it (foolish).
This shows that the same act can be viewed differently.
4
Understand the conclusion
Grasp that the act as an accident or movement is not inherently insulting; blame is on the doer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الآيات فقد بيّنا وهمه فيها، وحصوله على الدعوى كهو في هذا. وما ذكر من أنه شتم نفسه وكفر به ونحو هذا، فهو الذي لم يزل يعود نفسه من الكذب على خصومه. وليس أحد منهم يقول ذلك. بل لو خلق شتم نفسه يكون مشتوما في الحقيقة مذموما. بل خلق فعل الشتم من الكافر كذبًا وجورًا وسفها، وفي ذلك دفع كونه مشتوما مذموما في الحقيقة. ألا ترى أن من عرف فعل الشتم كذلك يكون عالما حكيما، ومن أخبره عنه كذلك يكون صادقاً؛ ومن عرفه على ما عليه عند الكافر كان جاهلاً سفيها، وبالخبر به كذلك يكون كاذبا، فمثله الذي ذكر ولا قوة إلا بالله وجملته أن فعله من حيث كان عرضاً أو شيئًا أو دليلاً على سفهه أو حركة ونحو ذلك لا يوصف بشتم ولا قبح، فمثله من وجه خلقه إياه. ولا قوة إلا بالله. وما قال من قتل أنابهم الأنبياء، فهو فيما أنا بهم موجود، وفيما أبقى أعداءه قائم؛ ثم لم يخرج ذلك من الحكمة. بل استدل إخوانه أن الذي يفعل هذا غير حكيم، فما الذي يجيبهم فهو في الأول جواب. وقوله: لم يكن في عهد رسول الله كذا، فكأنه قال: لا يجوز ورود البيان في الشيء قبل وقوعه، وأن البيان لا يرد فيما لم يسبق فيه التنازع. وذلك يدفع جميع آيات القرآن وما عليه الأمر المعتاد. وبعد، فإن الآية لو نزلت فيهم النزلت في ذمهم، ووصفت فيما نفوا عن الله من الوجه الذي نفاه أهل الاعتزال، فذلك لازم لهم. مع أن الآية لا يعمل بها المعتزلة من ذلك الوجه الذي لا يوجد في أصل دينهم جواز إضافة حقيقة ذلك إلى الله. فكيف يحتج على منكر مثله ممن يزعم أن ذلك في العقل مدفوع وطريقه السمع، ومحال الاحتجاج بالسمع على إمكانه في العقل؟ ثبت أن حقيقة ذلك في أفعال الخلق، وبه يكون امتداح في الحقيقة من وجوه أحدها في جعل كل شيء بحيث القدرة تحت قدرة الله، ليظهر حاجة الخلق جملة إلى الله تعالى في كون كل شيء لهم به. والثاني أن الوصف بالقدرة على ما لا فعل فيه لغيره ليس بعجيب، بل يستحقه كل ضعيف مهان، ثبت أن الامتداح يكون هذا الوجه. والثالث فيه بيان سفه من يفهم أن خلق كل شيء على ما عليه وصف الرب به أو تحقيق الفعل من الوجه الذي يكون من العباد منه. والرابع ليعلم أن الله لا يلحقه ذم في فعل أو مدح، من حيث ذلك المفعول، بحال. وذلك ينقض الاعتزال.
We have already explained his error in the verses, and his attainment of the claim is like that in this. And what he mentioned about insulting himself and disbelieving in it and similar things, that is what he never ceases to accuse himself of lying against his opponents. And not one of them says that. Rather, if he created the insult of himself, he would be insulted in reality and blameworthy. Rather, the creation of the act of insult from the disbeliever is lying, injustice, and foolishness, and in that is a repudiation of his being insulted and blameworthy in reality. Do you not see that whoever knows the act of insult in this way is knowing and wise? And whoever informs about it likewise is truthful. And whoever knows it as it is in the view of the disbeliever is ignorant and foolish, and by reporting it likewise he is a liar. So his example is what was mentioned, and there is no power except with Allah. Its summary is that his act, insofar as it is an accident or a thing or an evidence of his foolishness or a movement and the like, is not described as insult or ugliness. So his example is from the perspective of His creating it. There is no power except with Allah. And what he said about killing the prophets who killed them, that is in what I am with them existing, and in what He left of His enemies standing; then that does not remove it from wisdom. Rather, his brothers argued that the one who does this is not wise. So what is the answer to them? It is the first answer. And his saying: 'This was not in the time of the Messenger of Allah' is as if he said: 'It is not permissible for clarification to come before the occurrence of a thing, and that clarification does not come concerning what has not been disputed beforehand.' That repudiates all the verses of the Qur'an and what is the customary matter. Moreover, if the verse had been revealed concerning them, it would have been revealed in blame of them, and it described, in what they denied of Allah, from the aspect that the people of i'tizal denied, so that is binding on them. Yet the verse is not applied by the Mu'tazila from that aspect, because in the foundation of their religion there is no permissibility of attributing the reality of that to Allah. So how can one argue against a denier of such a thing, among those who claim that this is repudiated in reason and its path is revelation, and it is impossible to argue by revelation for its possibility in reason? It is established that the reality of that is in the acts of creatures, and by it there is praise in reality from aspects: one is that everything is made such that power is under the power of Allah, so that the need of all creatures for Allah Almighty appears in the existence of everything for them. The second is that the description of power over what no act belongs to others is not wondrous, rather every weak and despised one deserves it. It is established that praise is from this aspect. The third is that in it is a demonstration of the foolishness of one who understands that the creation of everything as it is is a description of the Lord, or the actualization of the act from the aspect that is from servants. The fourth is that it may be known that Allah is not affected by blame in an act or praise, from the perspective of that object, in any case. And that refutes i'tizal.
Source pages p. 327

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of a Mu'tazili argument about God's creation of evil. Maturidi begins by accusing his opponent (likely al-Ka'bi) of lying against his opponents—they never claimed that God insults Himself. He then argues that if God created an act of insult from a disbeliever, the act is lying, injustice, and foolishness from the disbeliever's side, not from God. God, knowing the act as it truly is, is wise and truthful. The act itself, being an accident or movement, is not inherently insulting. The blame attaches to the doer, not the creator of the doer. Next, he addresses the objection that prophets were killed by God's decree, yet this does not remove God's wisdom. He refutes the claim that such matters did not occur in the Prophet's time, arguing that this would invalidate the Qur'an which often clarifies events before they happen. He then turns to a specific verse that the Mu'tazila misinterpret to deny that God creates evil. He shows their inconsistency: they deny attributing the reality of created acts to God, yet they use revelation to prove such attribution is impossible. This is circular. Finally, he presents four aspects that demonstrate why God's creation of all acts is praiseworthy: (1) it shows all creatures' dependence on God; (2) true power is over acts that others have no power over; (3) it exposes the foolishness of those who misunderstand God's creation; (4) it shows that God is beyond praise or blame from His acts. This refutes the Mu'tazila.

Key Terms
شتم
خلق الأفعال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God becomes blameworthy for creating evil acts.
Correction: The act's blame is on the doer, not the creator. The act itself (as an accident) is not inherently insulting.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, why is it wrong to say that God's creation of an act of insult from a disbeliever makes God blameworthy?
A) Because the act is not really an insult from the disbeliever
B) Because the act, as an accident or movement, is not inherently insulting; blame attaches to the doer
C) Because God cannot create evil
D) Because the disbeliever does not actually commit the insult

Key Takeaway
God is not blamed for creating evil acts; blame is on the creature who performs them.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you ever find yourself mentally blaming God for putting you in that situation or for giving you the ability to sin? After this lesson, what specific thought will you replace that with the next time you are tempted to shift blame?
?
The passage says that knowing the act as it is makes one wise, and knowing it as the disbeliever does makes one foolish. In your own life, is there a sin you have been justifying or minimizing? Are you willing to see it as the foolish act it really is, and take full responsibility?
?
Imagine you are standing before Allah, and He asks you about a sin you committed. Would your response be to point to Him as the creator of the act, or to acknowledge your own fault? Write one concrete action you will take today to live out the truth that blame is entirely yours.

God's Wisdom in the Death of Prophets and the Nature of Clarification
Maturidi addresses objections about prophets' death and timing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that God's decree of prophets' death does not contradict His wisdom, and that clarification can precede occurrence.

Core Idea
God's actions, even if seemingly harmful, remain wise.

Maturidi addresses two objections: that God's killing of prophets implies lack of wisdom, and that such matters did not occur in the Prophet's time. He refutes both, showing that God's wisdom is intact and that revelation can clarify before events happen.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation to follow Maturidi's responses to the objections.
The text contains an objection and its refutation.
2
Identify the first objection
Find where the opponent argues that God's killing prophets shows He is not wise.
3
Understand Maturidi's response
Notice that Maturidi says this does not remove God's wisdom and refers to a previous answer.
He implies that God's wisdom is beyond human comprehension.
4
Identify the second objection
The opponent says such matters did not happen in the Prophet's time, implying they cannot happen.
5
Understand the refutation
Maturidi argues that clarification can come before an event, as in the Quran, and that this objection invalidates many verses.

?

?

The Praiseworthiness of God's Creation of All Acts: Four Aspects
Maturidi lists four aspects proving God's creation of all acts is praiseworthy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four reasons why God's creation of all acts is praiseworthy, and how this refutes the Mu'tazila.

Core Idea
God's creation of acts is praiseworthy because it demonstrates His power and the creature's need.

Maturidi concludes by establishing that the reality of acts is in creatures, and that God's creation of them is praiseworthy from four aspects. This final passage refutes the Mu'tazilite position entirely.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation to grasp the four aspects and their implications.
This part is enumerative; note the structure.
2
Identify the four aspects
Find each aspect: (1) power under God's power showing need, (2) true power, (3) exposes foolishness, (4) God beyond blame/praise.
3
Understand each aspect
Reflect on how each aspect shows God's praiseworthiness.
Consider the logical flow.
4
Connect to refutation of i'tizal
See how these aspects refute the Mu'tazili position that God's creation of evil cannot be praised.

الآيات فقد بيّنا وهمه فيها، وحصوله على الدعوى كهو في هذا. وما ذكر من أنه شتم نفسه وكفر به ونحو هذا، فهو الذي لم يزل يعود نفسه من الكذب على خصومه. وليس أحد منهم يقول ذلك. بل لو خلق شتم نفسه يكون مشتوما في الحقيقة مذموما. بل خلق فعل الشتم من الكافر كذبًا وجورًا وسفها، وفي ذلك دفع كونه مشتوما مذموما في الحقيقة. ألا ترى أن من عرف فعل الشتم كذلك يكون عالما حكيما، ومن أخبره عنه كذلك يكون صادقاً؛ ومن عرفه على ما عليه عند الكافر كان جاهلاً سفيها، وبالخبر به كذلك يكون كاذبا، فمثله الذي ذكر ولا قوة إلا بالله وجملته أن فعله من حيث كان عرضاً أو شيئًا أو دليلاً على سفهه أو حركة ونحو ذلك لا يوصف بشتم ولا قبح، فمثله من وجه خلقه إياه. ولا قوة إلا بالله. وما قال من قتل أنابهم الأنبياء، فهو فيما أنا بهم موجود، وفيما أبقى أعداءه قائم؛ ثم لم يخرج ذلك من الحكمة. بل استدل إخوانه أن الذي يفعل هذا غير حكيم، فما الذي يجيبهم فهو في الأول جواب. وقوله: لم يكن في عهد رسول الله كذا، فكأنه قال: لا يجوز ورود البيان في الشيء قبل وقوعه، وأن البيان لا يرد فيما لم يسبق فيه التنازع. وذلك يدفع جميع آيات القرآن وما عليه الأمر المعتاد. وبعد، فإن الآية لو نزلت فيهم النزلت في ذمهم، ووصفت فيما نفوا عن الله من الوجه الذي نفاه أهل الاعتزال، فذلك لازم لهم. مع أن الآية لا يعمل بها المعتزلة من ذلك الوجه الذي لا يوجد في أصل دينهم جواز إضافة حقيقة ذلك إلى الله. فكيف يحتج على منكر مثله ممن يزعم أن ذلك في العقل مدفوع وطريقه السمع، ومحال الاحتجاج بالسمع على إمكانه في العقل؟ ثبت أن حقيقة ذلك في أفعال الخلق، وبه يكون امتداح في الحقيقة من وجوه أحدها في جعل كل شيء بحيث القدرة تحت قدرة الله، ليظهر حاجة الخلق جملة إلى الله تعالى في كون كل شيء لهم به. والثاني أن الوصف بالقدرة على ما لا فعل فيه لغيره ليس بعجيب، بل يستحقه كل ضعيف مهان، ثبت أن الامتداح يكون هذا الوجه. والثالث فيه بيان سفه من يفهم أن خلق كل شيء على ما عليه وصف الرب به أو تحقيق الفعل من الوجه الذي يكون من العباد منه. والرابع ليعلم أن الله لا يلحقه ذم في فعل أو مدح، من حيث ذلك المفعول، بحال. وذلك ينقض الاعتزال.
We have already explained his error in the verses, and his attainment of the claim is like that in this. And what he mentioned about insulting himself and disbelieving in it and similar things, that is what he never ceases to accuse himself of lying against his opponents. And not one of them says that. Rather, if he created the insult of himself, he would be insulted in reality and blameworthy. Rather, the creation of the act of insult from the disbeliever is lying, injustice, and foolishness, and in that is a repudiation of his being insulted and blameworthy in reality. Do you not see that whoever knows the act of insult in this way is knowing and wise? And whoever informs about it likewise is truthful. And whoever knows it as it is in the view of the disbeliever is ignorant and foolish, and by reporting it likewise he is a liar. So his example is what was mentioned, and there is no power except with Allah. Its summary is that his act, insofar as it is an accident or a thing or an evidence of his foolishness or a movement and the like, is not described as insult or ugliness. So his example is from the perspective of His creating it. There is no power except with Allah. And what he said about killing the prophets who killed them, that is in what I am with them existing, and in what He left of His enemies standing; then that does not remove it from wisdom. Rather, his brothers argued that the one who does this is not wise. So what is the answer to them? It is the first answer. And his saying: 'This was not in the time of the Messenger of Allah' is as if he said: 'It is not permissible for clarification to come before the occurrence of a thing, and that clarification does not come concerning what has not been disputed beforehand.' That repudiates all the verses of the Qur'an and what is the customary matter. Moreover, if the verse had been revealed concerning them, it would have been revealed in blame of them, and it described, in what they denied of Allah, from the aspect that the people of i'tizal denied, so that is binding on them. Yet the verse is not applied by the Mu'tazila from that aspect, because in the foundation of their religion there is no permissibility of attributing the reality of that to Allah. So how can one argue against a denier of such a thing, among those who claim that this is repudiated in reason and its path is revelation, and it is impossible to argue by revelation for its possibility in reason? It is established that the reality of that is in the acts of creatures, and by it there is praise in reality from aspects: one is that everything is made such that power is under the power of Allah, so that the need of all creatures for Allah Almighty appears in the existence of everything for them. The second is that the description of power over what no act belongs to others is not wondrous, rather every weak and despised one deserves it. It is established that praise is from this aspect. The third is that in it is a demonstration of the foolishness of one who understands that the creation of everything as it is is a description of the Lord, or the actualization of the act from the aspect that is from servants. The fourth is that it may be known that Allah is not affected by blame in an act or praise, from the perspective of that object, in any case. And that refutes i'tizal.
Source pages p. 327

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of a Mu'tazili argument about God's creation of evil. Maturidi begins by accusing his opponent (likely al-Ka'bi) of lying against his opponents—they never claimed that God insults Himself. He then argues that if God created an act of insult from a disbeliever, the act is lying, injustice, and foolishness from the disbeliever's side, not from God. God, knowing the act as it truly is, is wise and truthful. The act itself, being an accident or movement, is not inherently insulting. The blame attaches to the doer, not the creator of the doer. Next, he addresses the objection that prophets were killed by God's decree, yet this does not remove God's wisdom. He refutes the claim that such matters did not occur in the Prophet's time, arguing that this would invalidate the Qur'an which often clarifies events before they happen. He then turns to a specific verse that the Mu'tazila misinterpret to deny that God creates evil. He shows their inconsistency: they deny attributing the reality of created acts to God, yet they use revelation to prove such attribution is impossible. This is circular. Finally, he presents four aspects that demonstrate why God's creation of all acts is praiseworthy: (1) it shows all creatures' dependence on God; (2) true power is over acts that others have no power over; (3) it exposes the foolishness of those who misunderstand God's creation; (4) it shows that God is beyond praise or blame from His acts. This refutes the Mu'tazila.

Key Terms
الامتداح
القدرة
الحاجة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God's creation of evil acts cannot be praiseworthy.
Correction: It is praiseworthy because it shows dependence, true power, exposes foolishness, and God is beyond blame.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, how many aspects demonstrate that God's creation of all acts is praiseworthy?
A) Two
B) Three
C) Four
D) Five

Key Takeaway
God's creation of all acts is praiseworthy for four reasons, refuting the Mu'tazila.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a painful trial or witness evil in the world, do you truly believe that God's creation of that act is praiseworthy? How does that belief challenge your immediate reaction of complaint or blame? Will you commit to reminding yourself of this truth next time you are tested?
?
Are you like the foolish one who thinks God's acts are similar to human acts, expecting God to be accountable to your standards? How can you train yourself to see God's absolute transcendence and instead respond with submission?
?
If God is not affected by praise or blame from His acts, why do you still fear people's judgment of your deeds? How does knowing that your very deeds are created by God free you from the need for human approval? What step can you take today to act only for God's pleasure?

The Witness Objection and Its Twofold Answer
Maturidi refutes the witness objection with two logical aspects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's two-part refutation of the objection that humans cannot distinguish the eternal from the temporal based on analogy with a witness.

Core Idea
Similarity is not ignorance—it is the ground for rational judgment.

In this passage, Maturidi addresses a clever objection: if a witness can fail to distinguish eternal from temporal, perhaps our reasoning about the two reeds is flawed. His answer unfolds in two clear aspects, each cutting to the heart of the objection. Let us examine them closely.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the full Arabic passage and its literal translation. Notice the objection and the two structured aspects of the answer.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the objection
The opponent compares the earlier reasoning about the reeds to a witness who cannot distinguish between eternal and temporal because he does not consider from the proper aspect.
This objection challenges the validity of the previous argument.
3
Examine the first aspect
Maturidi argues that in the original case (the reeds), there is no way to know the cause or to have certain knowledge about which reed is eternal, because we only see what is apparent. Therefore the objection has no force.
It denies any path to the cause in the first place.
4
Examine the second aspect
The second aspect states that the objection only works if one neglects the proper indication. In the reeds case, there is no distinguishing factor—the similarity stands as is.
The inability to distinguish is due to ignoring the right angle, not a flaw in the argument.
5
Reflect on the overall refutation
Consider how these two aspects together show that the objection does not undermine the original reasoning. The similarity of the two reeds remains a valid basis for judgment.
This reinforces Maturidi's method of reasoning from the witnessed to the unwitnessed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال : وهذا كمستدل بالشاهد، ربما يعجز عن الفصل بين القديم والحديث بما لم ينظر من وجهه، فمثله الأول. قال الفقيه رحمه الله : وذلك عليه لوجهين: أحدهما أن لا سبيل في الأول إلى السبب والعلم به في الحقيقة، مع ما ليس من الله غير الذي نراه ليُعلم به، فلا معنى لهذا إذا. الثاني أن الذي عارض به لا يجوز أن يكون على جهة واحدة تدل على أن عدم معرفة الحدث والقدم إنما هو في أنه لم ينظر إليه وأغفل عنه حيث لم ير موضع الدلالة. وما نحن فيه ليس ثمة ما يفصل، إن كان فهو في غيره. ثبت أنها بحيث [؟] أنفسهما شبيهان [؟] . ولا قوة إلا بالله .
He said: This is like one who seeks evidence from a witness, perhaps he is unable to distinguish between the eternal and the temporal due to not considering it from its aspect. So the like of the first. The Faqih (may God have mercy on him) said: And that applies to him from two aspects: the first is that there is no way in the first [case] to the cause and knowledge of it in reality, while there is from God nothing other than what we see to be known by it, so this has no meaning then. The second is that what he objected with cannot be on a single aspect indicating that the lack of knowledge of the temporal and the eternal is only due to his not looking at it and neglecting it where he did not see the place of indication. And what we are dealing with here, there is nothing that distinguishes; if there is, it is in other [things]. It is established that they are such that [؟] themselves are similar [؟]. And there is no power except through God.
Source pages p. 333

Commentary
This passage presents a second objection and its answer. The opponent compares the previous reasoning to a witness who fails to distinguish between eternal and temporal because he does not consider from the proper aspect. The answer (by الفقيه, possibly Abu'l-Qasim al-Hakim) provides two aspects. First, in the previous case (the reeds), there is no way to reach the cause and certain knowledge, and what we see from God is exactly what we perceive, so the objection is meaningless. Second, the opponent's objection is not valid from one single perspective; the inability to distinguish between eternal and temporal is due to neglecting the indication. In the case at hand (the reeds), there is no distinguishing factor; if there were, it would be in other examples. Thus, the two reeds remain similar in themselves.

Key Terms
شاهد (shahid/witness)
قديم (qadim)
حديث (hadith)
دلالة (dalala/indication)
سبب (sabab)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the answer concedes agnosticism about the reeds, implying we cannot know anything.
Correction: The answer actually affirms that the similarity itself is a rational basis; the objection fails because it either demands knowledge of the cause where none is available or neglects the proper indication.

Checkpoint
What are the two aspects of the answer to the witness objection?
A) The first aspect says there is a known cause; the second says the objection is correct
B) The first aspect denies any path to the cause; the second says the objection is based on neglect of indication
C) The first aspect affirms the witness's ability; the second denies similarity
D) The first aspect says God is unknowable; the second says the objection is invalid

Key Takeaway
Maturidi's twofold answer shows that the objection fails because it either demands knowledge of the cause where none is available or it neglects the proper indication.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you find yourself unable to distinguish between two seemingly similar things in your faith—like the attributes of God versus creation—do you immediately assume rational failure, or do you stop to consider that maybe you are not looking from the right 'aspect' (dhāt al-dalāla)? What does this say about your intellectual humility before God?
?
Maturidi insists that similarity itself is the ground for judgment, not confusion. Is there an area in your life where you have mistaken God's signs (like the order of creation) as meaningless coincidence rather than as clear indications? What would change if you saw them as the very proof you need?
?
The objection demanded knowledge of a 'cause' that God has not given us. Are there questions you insist on having answered—like 'why does God allow suffering?'—for which you demand a cause, even though God has not provided it? Will you submit to the sufficiency of what He has shown you, or will you remain in futile objection?

Disagreement on Whether Power Fits Both Obedience and Disobedience
Maturidi presents the disagreement and the argument for power being fit for both obedience and disobedience.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the disagreement about whether the power for obedience is also fit for disobedience, and the logical consequences that follow if power is not fit for both.

Core Idea
Power must fit both obedience and disobedience to avoid obligating the impossible.

This passage explores a key point of theological debate: Does the ability to obey also enable disobedience? Maturidi presents the view of Abu Hanifa and others that it does, and then shows that if power were limited to one action, it would lead to the problematic doctrine of obligating what is beyond capacity. Understanding this argument is crucial for grasping the Maturidi position on human capacity and divine command.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation to grasp the flow of the disagreement and argument.
Notice that Maturidi begins by stating a difference of opinion.
2
Identify the two positions
The passage presents two groups: those who say power fits both obedience and disobedience (Abu Hanifa and others) and the implied opposite view. Identify what the Mu'tazila holds upon reflection.
The Mu'tazila is said to affirm the same view implicitly.
3
Trace the logical argument
Follow the reasoning: every cause fits its thing and its opposite, so power (a cause) must fit both. If not, one would lose ability for the opposite act, making command and prohibition beyond capacity. Understand why this leads to the necessity of power being fit for both.
The argument uses the principle of 'fit' (salahiyya).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم اختلف أهل هذا القول في قوة الطاعة أهي تصلح للمعصية أم لا؟ قال جماعة: هي تصلح للأمرين جميعا، وهو قول أبي حنيفة وجماعة. وهذا القول أثبته جميع أهل الاعتزال عند التأمل، ويُحقق عليهم القول بتكليف ما لا يطاق، وذلك سببهم في القول بتقدم القوة. والله الموفق. وأصل هذا أنه لما كان كل سبب من أسباب الفعل يصلح للشيء وضده فكذلك القدرة - مع ما في نفي أن تصلح للأمرين فوت القدرة على فعل ضد الذي جاء به، وقد يؤمر به وينهى عنه في وقته - فيلزم القول بالقدرة على الشيء وضده، ليكون الأمر والنهي على الوسع والقوة. ولا قوة إلا بالله.
Then the people of this opinion differed concerning the power of obedience: is it fit for disobedience or not? A group said: it is fit for both matters entirely, and this is the saying of Abu Hanifa and a group. And this saying is affirmed by all the people of Mu'tazila upon reflection, and the saying of obligation of what is beyond capacity (taklif ma la yutaq) is established against them, and that is their cause in the saying of precedence of power (qudra). And Allah is the giver of success. And the origin of this is that since every cause of the causes of the act is fit for the thing and its opposite, likewise power (qudra) — along with what is in the negation that it is fit for both matters is the loss of power over the opposite of that which it brings, and it may be commanded and prohibited in its time — so it is necessary to affirm power over the thing and its opposite, so that command and prohibition are within capacity and power. And there is no power except from Allah.
Source pages p. 347

Commentary
This passage states the disagreement among scholars regarding whether the power (qudra) that enables obedience is also sufficient for disobedience. It begins by noting that some, including Abu Hanifa and a group, hold that it is fit for both. The author observes that all Mu'tazila implicitly affirm this view upon examination, which leads to the conclusion that they are committed to the doctrine of obligating what is beyond capacity (taklif ma la yutaq), as they also affirm the precedence of power. The core argument is then presented: Since every cause of an act is fit for both the act and its opposite, power (being a cause) must likewise be fit for both. If power were not fit for both, it would result in an inability to perform the opposite of an act, even when one may be commanded to do one thing and prohibited from another at the same time. Therefore, one must affirm that power extends to both the act and its opposite, ensuring that both command and prohibition fall within one's capacity. The passage ends with the formula 'There is no power except from Allah.'

Key Terms
قوة الطاعة
تصلح
القدرة
تكليف ما لا يطاق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Abu Hanifa and the Mu'tazila agree on the same concept of power.
Correction: The passage shows that while both affirm power fits both, the Mu'tazila's position leads to taklif ma la yutaq and the belief in precedence of power, which Maturidi opposes.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what follows if power is not fit for both an act and its opposite?
A) The act would be by nature, not choice.
B) The person would lose the ability to perform the opposite act.
C) The command and prohibition would be beyond capacity.
D) The person would be forced to perform both acts simultaneously.

Key Takeaway
Power must be capable of both obedience and disobedience to stay within human capacity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a command of Allah that you have been avoiding because you feel you lack the strength to obey. This lesson teaches that power must be fit for both obedience and its opposite. In light of this, is your feeling of 'I can't' a genuine limitation or an excuse? What specific step will you take today to act on that command, trusting that the same power enables both action and inaction?
?
When you sin, do you ever blame your circumstances or your 'limited capacity'? The passage argues that power itself is not the issue—if power were limited to one act, obedience would be impossible. How does this truth confront your excuses for disobedience? Write down one recurring sin and the excuse you use, then replace that excuse with a commitment to seek Allah's power (لا قوة إلا بالله).
?
This lesson shows that even the Mu'tazila, upon reflection, admit that power fits both obedience and disobedience, yet they hold a contradictory view. Are there any beliefs or habits in your life where your actions contradict what you know to be true? Challenge yourself this week to align one area of inconsistency with the truth of 'power over the thing and its opposite'.

If Power Were Not Fit for Both Acts Would Be by Nature
Maturidi states a principle and applies it to power.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational principle that if power is not fit for both ends, acts would be by nature, and why this matters for free will and moral responsibility in Maturidi theology.

Core Idea
Power must be fit for opposites to preserve choice.

This short passage from Imam Maturidi establishes a foundational rational principle: any capacity that is fit only for one specific outcome produces that outcome by natural necessity, not voluntary choice. He applies this to human power, arguing that if our power were not equally capable of both obedience and disobedience, our actions would be compelled, undermining moral accountability. Let's examine the text and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the concise logical structure.
2
Identify the general principle
Find the principle Maturidi states about 'everything that is fit for a thing and not its opposite'. What does he say about such a thing?
3
Apply it to power (quwwa)
Understand the conditional: if power were not fit for both acts (obedience and disobedience), then what would be the result?
This is the core application.
4
Reflect on the theological significance
Why is it important for human responsibility that power be fit for opposites? What would happen if it were not?
Consider the implications for moral accountability.
5
Conclude with the reminder
The passage ends with 'And there is no power except from Allah'. How does this affirmation relate to the argument?
This ties human capacity to divine origin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم الأصل أن كل شيء يصلح لشيء ولا يصلح لضده يكون الذي به بالطبع لا بالاختيار، ولو كانت القوة لا تصلح لهما لكان ما كان يقع بالطبع لا بالاختيار. ولا قوة إلا بالله.
Then the principle is that everything that is fit for a thing and not fit for its opposite is that by which it occurs by nature (tab') not by choice (ikhtiyar). And if power (al-quwwa) were not fit for both, then whatever occurs would occur by nature, not by choice. And there is no power except from Allah.
Source pages p. 347

Commentary
This passage states a foundational principle: If something is only capable of producing one specific effect and not its opposite, then the resulting effect occurs by natural compulsion (bi al-tab'), not by voluntary choice (bi al-ikhtiyar). The author applies this to the question of power (quwwa): if power were not fit for both obedience and disobedience, then any act that occurs would happen by necessity, not by free choice. This would undermine the moral responsibility that is essential in Islamic theology. The passage concludes with the reminder that all power is from Allah alone.

Key Terms
بالطبع (bi al-tab')
بالاختيار (bi al-ikhtiyar)
القوة (al-quwwa)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That 'by nature' here implies Maturidi is endorsing determinism or that all acts are naturally determined.
Correction: Maturidi is actually showing the negative consequence if power were not fit for both opposites: it would lead to acts being by nature, which undermines moral responsibility. He argues that power must be fit for both to preserve choice and accountability.

Checkpoint
What does the passage establish as the consequence if power is not fit for both an act and its opposite?
A) Both acts would be possible.
B) Acts would occur by choice.
C) Acts would occur by nature, not choice.
D) Power would be increased.

Key Takeaway
For human acts to be voluntary, power must be equally capable of producing the act or its opposite; otherwise, actions would be compelled by nature, negating moral responsibility.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you weigh a choice between obedience and disobedience, do you genuinely feel your power is equally fit for both? Or do you sense a pull that makes one easier? How does Maturidi's principle confront the excuses you make about your own sins?
?
If you truly believed that every action you do is either by nature or by choice, which category would most of your daily habits fall into? What would it cost you to shift one habit from 'by nature' to 'by choice' for the sake of Allah?
?
The passage ends with 'لا قوة إلا بالله'. In what areas of your life have you been acting as if your power were independent of Allah? Will you stop and acknowledge His grant of power before your next decision?
